\doxysection{oomph\+::Node Class Reference}
\hypertarget{classoomph_1_1Node}{}\label{classoomph_1_1Node}\index{oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}


Nodes are derived from \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Data}{Data}, but, in addition, have a definite (Eulerian) position in a space of a given dimension.  




{\ttfamily \#include $<$nodes.\+h$>$}

NPosition\+\_\+type is the number of coordinate types needed in the mapping between local and global coordinates (e.\+g. 1 for Lagrange-\/type elements; 2 for 1D Hermite elements; 4 for 2D Hermite elements, etc). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Helper function that should be overloaded derived classes that contain copies of data. The function must unset (NULL out) the internal pointers to the copied data. This is used when destructing data to ensure that all pointers remain valid. \doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Nodes are derived from \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Data}{Data}, but, in addition, have a definite (Eulerian) position in a space of a given dimension. 

The nodal coordinates are used in the elements\textquotesingle{} mapping between local and global coordinates and in the simplest case (stationary nodes in Lagrange-\/type elements) this mapping is given by \[ x_i = \sum_{j=1}^{N_{node}} X_{ij} \psi_{j}(s_k) \] so we need only access to the nodal coordinates $ X_{ij}\ (i=1..DIM) $ of all nodes $ j $ \+: provided by the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node} member function 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1Node_ab76b4773a65b349f143539e07b6e15e2}{Node::x}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_adb50e893b86b3e55e751a42eab3cba82}{i}})\ }

\end{DoxyCode}


If the nodal positions are time-\/dependent, the mapping becomes \[ x_i(t) = \sum_{j=1}^{N_{node}} X_{ij}(t) \ \psi_{j}(s_k). \] Within the computation (where time is only evaluated at discrete levels) this becomes \[ x_{ti} = \sum_{j=1}^{N_{node}} X_{ijt} \ \psi_{j}(s_k). \] and we need access to the nodal coordinates $ X_{ijt} \ (i=1..DIM) $ of all nodes $ j $ at the present (t=0) and previous (t\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0) timesteps\+: provided by the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node} member function 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1Node_ab76b4773a65b349f143539e07b6e15e2}{Node::x}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_af6f0bd3dc13317f895c91323c25c2b8f}{t}},\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_adb50e893b86b3e55e751a42eab3cba82}{i}})\ }

\end{DoxyCode}
 {\bfseries{Note\+:}} The interpretation of the history values is slightly more subtle than that. Depending on the positional \doxylink{classoomph_1_1TimeStepper}{Time\+Stepper} used, only a limited number of the positional history values accessed {\ttfamily Node\+::x(t,i)} represent previous nodal positions; the others are generalised history values that the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1TimeStepper}{Time\+Stepper} uses to determine approximations for the time-\/derivatives of the nodal positions.

Finally, some elements employ mappings that involve additional, generalised coordinates. For instance, in Hermite elements the mapping between local and global coordinates is based on an independent interpolation for the global coordinates and their derivative w.\+r.\+t. to the local coordinates. In such elements, the mapping becomes \[ x_i = \sum_{j=1}^{N_{node}} \sum_{k=1}^{N_{type}} X_{ijk} \psi_{jk}(s_k) \] where $ N_{type} $ is the number of the different types of generalised coordinates involved in the mapping. For instance, in 1D Hermite elements $ N_{type}=2 $ and k=0 corresponds to the global coordinates while k=1 corresponds to the derivative of the global coordinates w.\+r.\+t. to the local coordinate. In such cases we need access to the generalised nodal coordinates $ X_{ijk}  \ (i=1..DIM, \ k=1..N_{type}) $ of all nodes $ j $. Access is provided by the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node} member function 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1Node_af7fdc0dfda495d69bd31c790ee77da73}{Node::x\_gen}}(k,\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_adb50e893b86b3e55e751a42eab3cba82}{i}})\ }

\end{DoxyCode}
 and the corresponding time-\/dependent version 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1Node_af7fdc0dfda495d69bd31c790ee77da73}{Node::x\_gen}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_af6f0bd3dc13317f895c91323c25c2b8f}{t}},k,\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_adb50e893b86b3e55e751a42eab3cba82}{i}})\ }

\end{DoxyCode}
 While this is all pretty straightforward, it does make the argument list of the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node} constructors rather lengthy. 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source_l00905}{905}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source}{nodes.\+h}}.

Return the vector of the k-\/th generalised boundary coordinates on mesh boundary b. Broken virtual interface provides run-\/time error checking. 

Interface for function to get the k-\/th generalised boundary coordinate of the node on boundary b. Broken here in order to provide run-\/time error reporting. Must be overloaded by all boundary nodes. 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8cc_source_l02379}{2379}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8cc_source}{nodes.\+cc}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{void}} oomph\+::\+Node\+::make\+\_\+periodic (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{const}} \&}]{node\+\_\+pt }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}}



Make the node periodic by copying the values from node\+\_\+pt. Note that the coordinates will always remain independent, even though this may lead to (a little) unrequired information being stored. Broken virtual (only implemented in Boundary\+Nodes)

\Hypertarget{classoomph_1_1Node_aecf8c979266300d3609de2b4ddfa3cc8}\label{classoomph_1_1Node_aecf8c979266300d3609de2b4ddfa3cc8} 
\index{oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}!node\_update@{node\_update}}
\index{node\_update@{node\_update}!oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{node\_update()}{node\_update()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{virtual}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{void}} oomph\+::\+Node\+::node\+\_\+update (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{const}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{bool}} \&}]{update\+\_\+all\+\_\+time\+\_\+levels\+\_\+for\+\_\+new\+\_\+node = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{false}}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}



Interface for functions that update the nodal position using algebraic remeshing strategies. The interface is common to Spine\+Nodes, Algebraic\+Nodes and Macro\+Element\+Node\+Update\+Nodes. The default is that the node does not "{}update itself"{} i.\+e. it is fixed in space. When implemented, this function should also execute the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node}{Node}\textquotesingle{}s auxiliary node update function (if any). 



Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1AlgebraicNode_a754dc8fcac3382a07f60262c9792c84c}{oomph\+::\+Algebraic\+Node}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1MacroElementNodeUpdateNode_a02adaf04277672fd0e1be5296e6ed6cf}{oomph\+::\+Macro\+Element\+Node\+Update\+Node}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1SolidNode_ae66793af1a576edd29523ffb98b7225c}{oomph\+::\+Solid\+Node}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1SpineNode_afc47a59bee4ca3e42a56545afe20876d}{oomph\+::\+Spine\+Node}}.

\Hypertarget{classoomph_1_1Node_a98b3e63390c43196db9429f32319b0ca}\label{classoomph_1_1Node_a98b3e63390c43196db9429f32319b0ca}

\index{set\_hanging\_pt@{set\_hanging\_pt}!oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_hanging\_pt()}{set\_hanging\_pt()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{void}} oomph\+::\+Node\+::set\+\_\+hanging\+\_\+pt (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1HangInfo}{Hang\+Info}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{const}} \&}]{hang\+\_\+pt,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{const}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{int}} \&}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Set the hanging data for the i-\/th value. (hang\+\_\+pt=0 to make non-\/hanging) 

Set the hanging data for the i-\/th value. If node is already hanging, simply overwrite the appropriate entry. If the node isn\textquotesingle{}t hanging (because it might not be hanging geometrically), create the \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Vector}{Vector} of hanging pointers and make the other entries point to the node\textquotesingle{}s geometric hanging data. Set hang\+\_\+pt=0 to make entry explicitly non-\/hanging. Use \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node_a2517b670b4494f5421f5ec0d92cf8bb0}{Node\+::set\+\_\+nonhanging()} to unhang everything and clear up storage. 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8cc_source_l02068}{2068}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8cc_source}{nodes.\+cc}}.

\Hypertarget{classoomph_1_1Node_a9621d9d4dda3ebfe9578c180c5251484}\label{classoomph_1_1Node_a9621d9d4dda3ebfe9578c180c5251484} 
\index{oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}!Hanging\_pt@{Hanging\_pt}}
\index{Hanging\_pt@{Hanging\_pt}!oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Hanging\_pt}{Hanging\_pt}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1HangInfo}{Hang\+Info}}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} oomph\+::\+Node\+::\+Hanging\+\_\+pt\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}



C-\/style array of pointers to hanging node info. It\textquotesingle{}s set to NULL if the node isn\textquotesingle{}t hanging. The first entry (0) is the geometric hanging node data. The remaining entries correspond to the hanging data for the other values stored at the node. Usually, these entries will be the same as the geometric hanging node data represented by Hanging\+\_\+pt\mbox{[}0\mbox{]}, but this is not necessarily the case; e.\+g. the pressure in Taylor Hood has different hanging node data from the velocities. 



Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source_l00942}{942}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source}{nodes.\+h}}.

\index{oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}!No\_independent\_position@{No\_independent\_position}}
\index{No\_independent\_position@{No\_independent\_position}!oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{No\_independent\_position}{No\_independent\_position}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{unsigned}} oomph\+::\+Node\+::\+No\+\_\+independent\+\_\+position = 10\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}



Static "{}\+Magic number"{} used to indicate that there is no independent position in a periodic node. 

Static "{}\+Magic number"{} passed as independent\+\_\+position when there is no independent position in the periodic node. For example, in a periodic mesh. 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source_l00972}{972}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source}{nodes.\+h}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{unsigned}} oomph\+::\+Node\+::\+Nposition\+\_\+type\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}



Number of coordinate types used in the mapping between local and global coordinates (e.\+g. 1 for Lagrange-\/type elements; 2 for 1D Hermite elements; 4 for 2D Hermite elements, etc).

\Hypertarget{classoomph_1_1Node_a908941e709ac28995147ab090f2cbf90}\label{classoomph_1_1Node_a908941e709ac28995147ab090f2cbf90} 
\index{oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}!X\_position@{X\_position}}
\index{X\_position@{X\_position}!oomph::Node@{oomph::Node}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{X\_position}{X\_position}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classoomph_1_1TAdvectionDiffusionReactionElement}{double}}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} oomph\+::\+Node\+::\+X\+\_\+position\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}



Array of pointers to the data holding the Eulerian positions. The storage format must be the same as the internal data storage so that we can implement the functions \doxylink{classoomph_1_1Node_ab76b4773a65b349f143539e07b6e15e2}{x()} in generality here without the need for virtual functions. The first index will be a flat array of position types and coordinates and the second will be the number of time history values at each position type. 



Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source_l00929}{929}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{nodes_8h_source}{nodes.\+h}}.
